                             <span class="datetime secondary-text">
                              <a href="http://www.dailyacid.com/2009/12/11-us-presidents-but-only-1-queen.html?showComment=1259740185985#c2164798121270605911" rel="nofollow">

                            </div>
                            <p class="comment-content" id="bc_0_9MC">
                             Ill informed comments here and the writer of the article might not even know: the Queen of England actually has very limited power.
                             <br/>
                             <br/>
                             The country is run as a parliamentary democracy with a Prime Minister (Gordon Brown at the moment) as the most powerful member. Formally, the Queen heads the parliament and her opinion does have an effect, but her actual power is very much limited.
                             <br/>
                             <br/>
                             This is similar to the situation in many monarchies in Europe, including the one I live in: the Netherlands. Queen Beatrix has been our Queen since 1980, but we've went through many cabinets in the meantime, headed by a premier (Prime Minister) as well, currently Jan Peter Balkenende.
                             <br/>
                             <br/>
                             In most cases, the opinion is that monarchies are likely to fall, or rather turn into republics under public pressure, if ever the monarch should exert too much power. The army, the police, all are under power of the government, which in most cases is composed of elected officials.
                             <br/>
                             <br/>
                             The role of the royal families has been reduced to a diplomatical and ceremonial one. Be it an influential one, but you have to see this in the context of the golden cage these people have to live in...
                            </p>

This education of the masses occurred in the face of a culture marked by drunkenness, addiction to sensuality, lack of self-control, and lack of education whose model reached its pinnacle in the example of the sons of George III (who was king during the American Revolution).

                             <br/>
                             George IIIs granddaughter, Queen Victorias reign marked a new era of moral responsibility in government which Queen Elizabeth II has tried very hard to model.
                             <br/>
                             <br/>
                             Queen Elizabeths mother, who was from Scotland, was hugely popular for providing a stable home for her husband and children, her bravery in the face of Hitlers threats to kill them, and being able to relate to the common people who also had and have high moral standards.

                             The Queen whose titles include Defender of Faith has a distinct advantage over American culture whose persecution of believers is becoming more and more militant.
